  1  4 amended to read as follows:
  1  5    SEC. 27.  DEPARTMENT OF JUSTICE.
  1  6    1.  There is appropriated from the general fund of the state
  1  7 to the department of justice for the fiscal year beginning July
  1  8 1, 2018, and ending June 30, 2019, the following amounts, or
  1  9 so much thereof as is necessary, to be used for the purposes
  1 10 designated:
  1 11    a.  For the general office of attorney general for salaries,
  1 12 support, maintenance, and miscellaneous purposes, including
  1 13 the prosecuting attorneys training program, matching funds
  1 14 for federal violence against women grant programs, victim
  1 15 assistance grants, office of drug control policy prosecuting
  1 16 attorney program, and odometer fraud enforcement, and for not
  1 17 more than the following full=time equivalent positions:

 10 29 draw more than the amount appropriated in this subsection and
 10 30 incur a negative cash balance as long as there are receivables
 10 31 equal to or greater than the negative balance and the amount

 10 34    2.  The Iowa law enforcement academy may select at least
 10 35 five automobiles of the department of public safety, division
 11  1 of state patrol, prior to turning over the automobiles to
 11  2 the department of administrative services to be disposed
 11  3 of by public auction, and the Iowa law enforcement academy
 11  4 may exchange any automobile owned by the academy for each
 11  5 automobile selected if the selected automobile is used in
 11  6 training law enforcement officers at the academy. However, any
 11  7 automobile exchanged by the academy shall be substituted for
 11  8 the selected vehicle of the department of public safety and
 11  9 sold by public auction with the receipts being deposited in the
 11 10 depreciation fund to the credit of the department of public
 11 11 safety, division of state patrol.
 11 12    3.  The Iowa law enforcement academy shall provide training
 11 13 for domestic abuse and human trafficking=related issues
 11 14 throughout the state.  The training shall be offered at no
 11 15 cost to the attendees and the training shall not replace any
 11 16 existing domestic abuse or human trafficking training offered
 11 17 by the academy.

 10 35 five automobiles of the department of public safety, division

 23 27    Sec. 22.   23 27    Sec. 22.   23 28 ==== prohibitions.
 23 29    1.  As used in this section:
 23 30    a.  "Facility" means a county jail, municipal holding
 23 31 facility, secure facility for the detention or custody
 23 32 of juveniles, community=based correctional facility, or
 23 33 institution under the management of the department of
 23 34 corrections.
 23 35    b.  "Unmanned aerial vehicle" means a vehicle or device
 24  1 that uses aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted
 24  2 remotely.
 24  3    2.  A person shall not operate an unmanned aerial vehicle
 24  4 knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is operating in, on,
 24  5 or above a facility and any contiguous real property comprising
 24  6 the surrounding grounds of the facility, unless the unmanned
 24  7 aerial vehicle is operated by a law enforcement agency or the
 24  8 person has permission from the authority in charge of the
 24  9 facility to operate an unmanned aerial vehicle in, on, or above
 24 10 such facility.
 24 11    3.  A person who violates this section commits a class "D"
 24 12 felony.

 24 15    Sec. 23.   24 15    Sec. 23.   24 16    The court file containing the conviction for which an
 24 17 applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be part of the
 24 18 record in any action under this chapter.  Upon the filing
 24 19 of an application for postconviction relief pursuant to
 24 20 section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall make the
 24 21 underlying criminal file records accessible to the applicant,
 24 22 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 24 23 records are not available in electronic format, the clerk of
 24 24 the district court shall convert the records to an electronic
 24 25 format and make the records available to the applicant, county
 24 26 attorney, and attorney general.
 24 27                           EXPLANATION
 24 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
 24 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
 24 30    This bill relates to and makes appropriations to the justice
 24 31 system, and makes other related statutory changes.
 24 32    DIVISION I ==== FY 2018=2019 APPROPRIATIONS.  The bill makes
 24 33 appropriations from the general fund of the state for fiscal
 24 34 year 2018=2019 to the departments of justice, corrections,
 24 35 public defense, public safety, and homeland security and
 25  1 emergency management, and the Iowa law enforcement academy,
 25  2 office of the state public defender, board of parole, Iowa
 25  3 state civil rights commission, and the criminal and juvenile
 25  4 justice planning division of the department of human rights.
 25  5    The bill appropriates moneys from the department of commerce
 25  6 revolving fund to the office of consumer advocate of the
 25  7 department of justice for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25  8    The bill requires the division of criminal investigation
 25  9 to employ 4.00 full=time equivalent positions to assist in
 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.
 25 11    The bill appropriates moneys from the general fund of the
 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 24 17 applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be part of the
 24 18 record in any action under this chapter.  Upon the filing
 24 19 of an application for postconviction relief pursuant to
 24 20 section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall make the
 24 21 underlying criminal file records accessible to the applicant,
 24 22 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 24 23 records are not available in electronic format, the clerk of
 24 24 the district court shall convert the records to an electronic
 24 25 format and make the records available to the applicant, county
 24 26 attorney, and attorney general.
 24 27                           EXPLANATION
 24 28 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
 24 29 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
 24 30    This bill relates to and makes appropriations to the justice
 24 31 system, and makes other related statutory changes.
 24 32    DIVISION I ==== FY 2018=2019 APPROPRIATIONS.  The bill makes
 24 33 appropriations from the general fund of the state for fiscal
 24 34 year 2018=2019 to the departments of justice, corrections,
 24 35 public defense, public safety, and homeland security and
 25  1 emergency management, and the Iowa law enforcement academy,
 25  2 office of the state public defender, board of parole, Iowa
 25  3 state civil rights commission, and the criminal and juvenile
 25  4 justice planning division of the department of human rights.
 25  5    The bill appropriates moneys from the department of commerce
 25  6 revolving fund to the office of consumer advocate of the
 25  7 department of justice for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25  8    The bill requires the division of criminal investigation
 25  9 to employ 4.00 full=time equivalent positions to assist in
 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.
 25 11    The bill appropriates moneys from the general fund of the
 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.

 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 24 22 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 24 23 records are not available in electronic format, the clerk of
 24 24 the district court shall convert the records to an electronic
 24 25 format and make the records available to the applicant, county
 24 26 attorney, and attorney general.

 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.

 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.

 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn

 24 30    This bill relates to and makes appropriations to the justice
 24 31 system, and makes other related statutory changes.
 24 32    DIVISION I ==== FY 2018=2019 APPROPRIATIONS.  The bill makes
 24 33 appropriations from the general fund of the state for fiscal
 24 34 year 2018=2019 to the departments of justice, corrections,
 24 35 public defense, public safety, and homeland security and
 25  1 emergency management, and the Iowa law enforcement academy,
 25  2 office of the state public defender, board of parole, Iowa
 25  3 state civil rights commission, and the criminal and juvenile
 25  4 justice planning division of the department of human rights.
 25  5    The bill appropriates moneys from the department of commerce
 25  6 revolving fund to the office of consumer advocate of the
 25  7 department of justice for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25  8    The bill requires the division of criminal investigation
 25  9 to employ 4.00 full=time equivalent positions to assist in
 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.
 25 11    The bill appropriates moneys from the general fund of the
 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.

 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.

 26 11 safety.

 26 20 nudity.

 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 24 32    DIVISION I ==== FY 2018=2019 APPROPRIATIONS.  The bill makes
 24 33 appropriations from the general fund of the state for fiscal
 24 34 year 2018=2019 to the departments of justice, corrections,
 24 35 public defense, public safety, and homeland security and
 25  1 emergency management, and the Iowa law enforcement academy,
 25  2 office of the state public defender, board of parole, Iowa
 25  3 state civil rights commission, and the criminal and juvenile
 25  4 justice planning division of the department of human rights.
 25  5    The bill appropriates moneys from the department of commerce
 25  6 revolving fund to the office of consumer advocate of the
 25  7 department of justice for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25  8    The bill requires the division of criminal investigation
 25  9 to employ 4.00 full=time equivalent positions to assist in
 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.
 25 11    The bill appropriates moneys from the general fund of the
 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill

 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.

 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.

 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 25  2 office of the state public defender, board of parole, Iowa
 25  3 state civil rights commission, and the criminal and juvenile
 25  4 justice planning division of the department of human rights.
 25  5    The bill appropriates moneys from the department of commerce
 25  6 revolving fund to the office of consumer advocate of the
 25  7 department of justice for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25  8    The bill requires the division of criminal investigation
 25  9 to employ 4.00 full=time equivalent positions to assist in
 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.
 25 11    The bill appropriates moneys from the general fund of the
 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.

 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.

 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 25  8    The bill requires the division of criminal investigation
 25  9 to employ 4.00 full=time equivalent positions to assist in
 25 10 expediting the processing and analysis of DNA samples.
 25 11    The bill appropriates moneys from the general fund of the
 25 12 state to the criminalistics laboratory fund created in Code
 25 13 section 691.9 to accelerate the DNA analysis of DNA samples.
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.

 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 25 14    The bill requires the commissioner of the department of
 25 15 public safety to appoint an administrator of the fire service
 25 16 training bureau of the division of state fire marshal pursuant
 25 17 to Code section 100B.7 as a condition of appropriation to the
 25 18 division of state fire marshal.
 25 19    The bill also appropriates moneys from the gaming
 25 20 enforcement revolving fund to the department of public safety
 25 21 for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 22    The bill appropriates moneys from the wireless 911 emergency
 25 23 communications fund to the department of homeland security and
 25 24 emergency management for fiscal year 2018=2019.
 25 25    The bill appropriates moneys from the Iowa skilled worker
 25 26 and job creation fund to the department of corrections for
 25 27 implementation, support, maintenance, and capital construction
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill

 26 32 including county and city violations.

 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87

 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 25 28 costs to develop a regional housing building project.
 25 29    The bill appropriates moneys from the consumer education and
 25 30 litigation fund to the department of justice for farm mediation
 25 31 services and for criminal prosecutions, criminal appeals, and
 25 32 performing duties related to state tort claims.
 25 33    The bill strikes Code section 13.2(1)(g) requiring the
 25 34 attorney general to report to the governor, at the time
 25 35 provided by law, the condition of the attorney general's
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.

 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 26  1 office, opinions rendered, and business transacted of public
 26  2 interest.
 26  3    The bill establishes a public safety support trust fund
 26  4 in the state treasury under the control of the department of
 26  5 public safety.  The bill permits the department of public
 26  6 safety to receive and accept donations, grants, loans, and
 26  7 contributions from any public or private source for deposit
 26  8 into the trust fund.  Moneys credited to the trust fund are
 26  9 appropriated to the department of public safety for the purpose
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.

 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 26 10 of supporting the activities of the department of public
 26 11 safety.
 26 12    DIVISION II ==== PRISON LIBRARIES.  The bill strikes a
 26 13 provision requiring the director of the department of
 26 14 corrections to provide, as necessary, suitable space for
 26 15 reading material for inmates.  Additionally, the bill prohibits
 26 16 the department of corrections from using any appropriated funds
 26 17 or other funds made available to the department to distribute
 26 18 or make available any commercially published information or
 26 19 material to an inmate that is sexually explicit or features
 26 20 nudity.

       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn
 26 20 nudity.
 26 21    DIVISION III ==== SMALL CLAIMS JURISDICTION.  The bill makes
 26 22 jurisdictional changes to small claims court cases. The bill
 26 23 provides that a small claims court case commenced on or after
 26 24 July 1, 2018, shall not involve damages or value in excess of
 26 25 $7,500. Under existing law, a small claims court case shall
 26 26 not involve damages or value in excess of $5,000. The bill
 26 27 further provides that the jurisdictional amount shall revert
 26 28 to $5,000 if a court finds the $7,500 amount unconstitutional.
 26 29 By increasing the jurisdictional amount for small claims court
 26 30 the bill expands the jurisdiction of a magistrate or district
 26 31 associate judge to hear and assess judgment on certain actions,
 26 32 including county and city violations.
 26 33    DIVISION IV ==== UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES.  The bill defines
 26 34 "unmanned aerial vehicle" to mean a vehicle or device that uses
 26 35 aerodynamic forces to achieve flight and is piloted remotely.
 27  1 Under the bill, a person shall not operate an unmanned
 27  2 aerial vehicle knowing that the unmanned aerial vehicle is
 27  3 operating in, on, or above such a facility and any contiguous
 27  4 real property comprising the surrounding grounds of the
 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
       LSB 5032SV (2) 87
       jm/rn

 27  5 facility, unless the unmanned aerial vehicle is operated by a
 27  6 law enforcement agency or the person has permission from the
 27  7 authority in charge of the facility to operate an unmanned
 27  8 aerial vehicle in, on, or above such facility.
 27  9    A person who violates the bill commits a class "D" felony.  A
 27 10 class "D" felony is punishable by confinement for no more than
 27 11 five years and a fine of at least $750 but not more than $7,500.
 27 12    DIVISION V ==== POSTCONVICTION RELIEF.  The bill creates new
 27 13 Code section 822.10A relating to postconviction procedure.  The
 27 14 bill provides that the court file containing the conviction
 27 15 for which the applicant seeks postconviction relief shall be
 27 16 part of the record in any action under Code chapter 822.  Upon
 27 17 the filing of an application for postconviction relief pursuant
 27 18 to Code section 822.3, the clerk of the district court shall
 27 19 make the underlying criminal file accessible to the applicant,
 27 20 county attorney, and attorney general.  If the criminal file
 27 21 records are not available in electronic format, the division
 27 22 requires the clerk of the district court to convert the records
 27 23 to an electronic format and make the records available to the
 27 24 applicant, county attorney, and attorney general.
